<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8afd9a37-4a11-46b9-8efe-e8ae0fd1a6e7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText15253887247490231175" style="display:none">Detective Thursday Next has had her fill of her responsibilities as the Bellman in Jurisfiction. Packing up her son, Friday, Thursday returns to Swindon accompanied by none other than the dithering Danish prince Hamlet. But returning to SpecOps is no snap—as outlaw fictioneer Yorrick Kaine plots for absolute power, the return of Swindon's patron saint foretells doom, and if that isn't bad enough, back in the Book World <i>The Merry Wives of Windsor</i> is becoming entangled with <i>Hamlet</i>. Can Thursday find a Shakespeare clone to stop this hostile takeover? Can she vanquish Kaine and prevent the world from plunging into war? And, most important, will she ever find reliable childcare? Find out in this totally original, action-packed romp, sure to be another escapist thrill for Jasper Fforde's legion of fans.</span>

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_6581625').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

          });

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2319544698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319544698" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319544698?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=fforde-jasper">fforde-jasper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319544698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5662610670136075167">So here come some of the main ingredients of this part of the series of inimitable inter genre reading cocktails:<br/><br/>Propaganda, manipulation, and warmongering in politics and trade: the satirizing of all the conspiracy theories and real-life events in this regard play a key role in the series, as it´s often the evil corporation that is playing with the next attempt of real-world domination, literary world submission, or just mega sales of a new product, not caring about the potential causality, tim</span>
  <span id="freeText5662610670136075167" style="display:none">So here come some of the main ingredients of this part of the series of inimitable inter genre reading cocktails:<br /><br />Propaganda, manipulation, and warmongering in politics and trade: the satirizing of all the conspiracy theories and real-life events in this regard play a key role in the series, as it´s often the evil corporation that is playing with the next attempt of real-world domination, literary world submission, or just mega sales of a new product, not caring about the potential causality, time loop, stability of the whole book universe, consequences. Some of the funniest and most profound scenes and plot twists are created by using real-life inspired happenings.<br /><br />Hamlet has hardly ever gotten so many laughs instead of sighs, tears, and suffering. So it took four parts until we reached the soliloquizing skull wielder and I guess friends of Shakespeare (will hardly ever read it) may find much more pleasure than the average reader for whom there are wit, entertaining literary history, and some alternative plot use options for the old fellow.<br /><br />What happens if real, living genres merge or are forced to interbreed and get monstrous, dysfunctional, mad kids? This, one of Ffjordes´most ingenious ideas, has become one of my favorite creativity technique vehicle and, once again, I ask myself why nobody else before had this idea before Fforde. Parody and satire used the idea of mixing not fitting and opposed ideas together for millennia, I don´t know if there might not be even the one or other cave painting, but Ffjorde nailed it and pimped it to perfection. Try it, take 2 or 3 genres with 2 very different authors and bam, that´s brainstorming and creative writing ammunition for a long time.<br /><br />Literary detective rules and conventions of genres. Kind of relates to the last point and is one of the driving forces of the series, as Thursday is a mixture of different thriller genre tropes. But imagine it with another setting, this has a Pratchettian potential for more satire in close to every genre (except tragedy probably), or, my dream, to use the giant of satire again, Pratchett in space with sci-fi elements. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Goliath corporation as a religion, how cool is this? It also opens the question of where and if the differences between a religion and a profit and shareholder value-oriented company are and how much faith and belief there is in economics and fiat money in general, but we don´t want to get too reflective and have fun instead, jay.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Creator/JasperFforde">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/ThursdayNext">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5662610670136075167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/381149-martine?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/381149-martine?shelf=humour">humour</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12276038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14322180489010784913">The fouth instalment of the Thursday Next series is my favourite one, the one in which all the plotlines set out earlier are woven together and political satire enters the series in a grand way.<br/><br/>In <i>Something Rotten</i>, Thursday returns from the book world to late-1980s England with her two-year-old son, two dodos and the Prince of Denmark, Hamlet, who wishes to see a bit of the world. As it happens, Hamlet's arrival in the real world poses a bit of a problem, for unbeknownst to Thursday, a fictional</span>
  <span id="freeText14322180489010784913" style="display:none">The fouth instalment of the Thursday Next series is my favourite one, the one in which all the plotlines set out earlier are woven together and political satire enters the series in a grand way.<br /><br />In <i>Something Rotten</i>, Thursday returns from the book world to late-1980s England with her two-year-old son, two dodos and the Prince of Denmark, Hamlet, who wishes to see a bit of the world. As it happens, Hamlet's arrival in the real world poses a bit of a problem, for unbeknownst to Thursday, a fictional character, Yorrick Kaine, has been trying to get himself elected dictator of the British Isles, and he has just launched a vitriolic campaign against all things Danish, including Kierkegaard and <i>Out of Africa</i>. Just as worryingly, the almighty Goliath Corporation is trying to pass itself off as a religion rather than Big Brother, which, if everything goes according to plan, will change life in Britain significantly, and not for the better. Needless to say, Thursday has to sort things out, which she does while trying to evade an assassin, visiting the world of the dead and making sure that the local croquet team wins the cup, as the thirteenth-century saint St Zvlkx, who is always right, has predicted that the fate of the world depends on this match. Naturally, she also spends a bit of time trying to get back her husband, who still has an existence problem, but first she has to arrange a baby-sitter for her son, which proves just as difficult.<br /><br /><i>Something Rotten</i> gets off to a slow start, but once it gets under way (some 100 pages into the book), it's excellent; the second of half of the book may well be the best part of the series so far. The political satire is thick and hilarious, the cameos and conspiracy theories are great fun, the loose ends are tied up very nicely, and in the end, nearly everyone gets what he/she deserves. What more could a reader want?</span>
  <a data-text-id="14322180489010784913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText6727216658884393940" style="display:none">Have you started the Thursday Next series yet? <div id="review_2842490477" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2842490477" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7206839-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593734236p2/7206839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2842490477?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/7206839-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2842490477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15369093171516959203">I really enjoyed this installment in the Thursday Next series! It moved more quickly than The Well of Lost Plots, and there was some suspense. Overall, it’s the characters and the quirkiness that keep me invested in this series. I love Fforde’s writing style, his humor, and the literary allusions. I love that the series is postmodern surrealist science fiction. There’s time travel, strange technology, and visits to the underworld. Mythological characters feature as much as the characters of the </span>
  <span id="freeText15369093171516959203" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this installment in the Thursday Next series! It moved more quickly than The Well of Lost Plots, and there was some suspense. Overall, it’s the characters and the quirkiness that keep me invested in this series. I love Fforde’s writing style, his humor, and the literary allusions. I love that the series is postmodern surrealist science fiction. There’s time travel, strange technology, and visits to the underworld. Mythological characters feature as much as the characters of the literary canon. I like Fforde best when he mixes the Outland with the Book World. The clash of cultures is especially interesting to me, and it’s unique to have the characters travel back and forth whereas Thursday living fully in the Book World had less variety and felt more static. <br /><br />Overall, I liked this book a lot and think it continues Thursday’s story well. I was very relieved that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Landen is finally back! His being eradicated for so long was starting to get frustrating and repetitive <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It was great to see some villains get their comeuppance. Of course, there are parts I thought were a little boring or that were resolved too quickly, but the book is action packed and interesting throughout most of it. <br /><br />I definitely recommend this installment if you already like the series. If you haven’t read the first three books, you might be a little confused, but again, Fforde does a great job of explaining relevant key events, and if he doesn’t go into detail, it’s because the events aren’t as important to the plot. There’s also one major twist that I never saw coming that I thought was really clever. <br /><br />Again, I don’t know how far I’ll get in this series. I’ve given up on Alan Bradley’s Flavia de Luce series, which became too repetitive and trite for me, but I am still enjoying this series and will definitely read Book #5!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15369093171516959203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_863307242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863307242" />
    <a title="melydia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1264081-melydia"><img alt="melydia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226610198p2/1264081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863307242?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="melydia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="melydia" href="/user/show/1264081-melydia">melydia</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863307242" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5626066650681609480">With every book I've read in this series, I've said the same thing: this was fun but I doubt I'll continue on with the series. Well, this is the fourth book and I give up. I'm going to keep reading Thursday Next books because they're absolutely ridiculous and they make me laugh. This time around, Thursday is back in the real world, where she has to deal with fictional would-be dictators, semi-dead presidents, a husband who may not actually exist, violent cricket matches, 13th century mystics, a </span>
  <span id="freeText5626066650681609480" style="display:none">With every book I've read in this series, I've said the same thing: this was fun but I doubt I'll continue on with the series. Well, this is the fourth book and I give up. I'm going to keep reading Thursday Next books because they're absolutely ridiculous and they make me laugh. This time around, Thursday is back in the real world, where she has to deal with fictional would-be dictators, semi-dead presidents, a husband who may not actually exist, violent cricket matches, 13th century mystics, a perpetually dithering Hamlet, and - most daunting of all - motherhood. The whole thing is just marvelous. My favorite part was "Avoid the Question Time," which is pretty much what all political interviews and debates actually are but won't admit it. Nothing is too outlandish to show up in these stories, and I can't wait for the next book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8194133450773181380">4.5*<br/><i><br/>"I knocked at their door and, hearing no answer, walked in. When I was last working at SpecOps we rarely heard anything from the mildly eccentric members of the time-travelling elite, but when you work in the time business, you don’t waste it by nattering – it’s much too precious. My father always argued that time was far and away the most valuable commodity we had and that temporal profligacy should be a criminal offence – which kind of makes watching Celebrity Kidney Swap or reading Daphne</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8194133450773181380" style="display:none">4.5*<br /><i><br />"I knocked at their door and, hearing no answer, walked in. When I was last working at SpecOps we rarely heard anything from the mildly eccentric members of the time-travelling elite, but when you work in the time business, you don’t waste it by nattering – it’s much too precious. My father always argued that time was far and away the most valuable commodity we had and that temporal profligacy should be a criminal offence – which kind of makes watching Celebrity Kidney Swap or reading Daphne Farquitt novels a crime straight away."</i><br /><br />After being disappointed by book #2 and skipping book #3, I loved this one. Something Rotten had just the right mix of silliness with thoughtful digs at current affairs and contemporary discussions such as the argument about what makes humans human and what gives humans have the right to control other species, or the rights of other groups of humans for that matter.<br /> <br />Thursday has returned from the book world and again takes up the pursuit of a shady character that threatens the country. But, Thursday has not returned alone - Hamlet (aka the "ditherer") has come with her and so has Alan. I loved Alan, and I am having to read the rest of the series just to find out how he fares.<br /><br />Yes. Never mind Thursday and the fate of Landon, my interests in this series are thoroughly invested in Pickwick and Alan!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038861496" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7885554612158666363">Book on CD read by Emily Gray.<br/><br/>Book four in the Thursday Next fantasy / sci-fi “literary detective” series. The Goliath Corporation is still trying to take over the world, though this time their scheme is to be declared a religion. Hamlet is staying with Thursday and her family, while she tries to sort out the mess that all the cloned Shakespeares have made of the original play. Thursday’s father, the rogue ChronoGuard, and her mad-scientist Uncle Mycroft, both make significant, though small, con</span>
  <span id="freeText7885554612158666363" style="display:none">Book on CD read by Emily Gray.<br /><br />Book four in the Thursday Next fantasy / sci-fi “literary detective” series. The Goliath Corporation is still trying to take over the world, though this time their scheme is to be declared a religion. Hamlet is staying with Thursday and her family, while she tries to sort out the mess that all the cloned Shakespeares have made of the original play. Thursday’s father, the rogue ChronoGuard, and her mad-scientist Uncle Mycroft, both make significant, though small, contributions.<br /><br />What I most enjoy about this series is Fforde’s vivid imagination and all the literary references. The plots are completely unrealistic, but that’s part of the fun. Thursday is a strong, independent, resourceful heroine, and the supporting characters – Spike, the vampire, and Stig, the Neanderthal, in particular – are delightfully over-the-top. The SuperHoop (think “Super Bowl” for croquet) match is fun and thrilling and ridiculous all at once. <br /><br />If this review doesn’t make much sense … well, neither does the book. But who cares?! It’s fun to read. <br /><br />Emily Gray does a marvelous job performing the audio version. She has great pacing and is a skilled voice artist, able to differentiate the many characters. I love the way she voices Stig and St Zvlkx in this installment. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3265309406211562908">I regarded reading the 4th book in the series more like a duty, rather than something interesting to pass time with. I didn't really <em>want</em> to read it now, but since I got through the first 3 I might as well read the 4th one too, right? Plus I would've probably forgotten the plot in a year. In other words: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26999.Something_Rotten__Thursday_Next___4_' title='Something Rotten (Thursday Next, #4) by Jasper Fforde' rel='nofollow noopener'>Something Rotten</a> was bound for failure right from the beginning.<br/><br/>... and now <em>I</em>'m wondering if <em>I</em> could just possibly insert yet another <em>I</em> somewhere in this paragraph: <em>I</em>!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419274093ra/13025190.gif' alt='sorry bro' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Two years have passed since</span>
  <span id="freeText3265309406211562908" style="display:none">I regarded reading the 4th book in the series more like a duty, rather than something interesting to pass time with. I didn't really <em>want</em> to read it now, but since I got through the first 3 I might as well read the 4th one too, right? Plus I would've probably forgotten the plot in a year. In other words: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26999.Something_Rotten__Thursday_Next___4_" title="Something Rotten (Thursday Next, #4) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Rotten</a> was bound for failure right from the beginning.<br><br>... and now <em>I</em>'m wondering if <em>I</em> could just possibly insert yet another <em>I</em> somewhere in this paragraph: <em>I</em>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419274093ra/13025190.gif" alt="sorry bro" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Two years have passed since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27001.The_Well_of_Lost_Plots__Thursday_Next__3_" title="The Well of Lost Plots (Thursday Next #3) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Lost Plots</a> and Thursday is ready to go back to the <em>Real</em> World, and get her husband reactualized. Easier said than done. Her friends at Jurisfiction are not ready for a new Bellman, her son Friday needs a nanny, and 'back home' she's still very much a wanted criminal.<br><br>Since it never pours but rains, she finds that Yorrick Kaine (the villain from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27000.Lost_in_a_Good_Book__Thursday_Next___2_" title="Lost in a Good Book (Thursday Next, #2) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost in a Good Book</a>), is about to be elected a dictator for life. The evil multinational Goliath Corporation has decided to 'up the ante' by backing Kaine's candidacy and also angling to become a religion. <br><br>Luckily, <em>all</em> this can be avoided if the Swindon Mallets win the 1988 Superhoop. Too bad their players suck.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419274093ra/13025191.gif" alt="Yeah, OK" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have to admit, there are LOTS of hilarious moments, tonnes of memorable quotes, and the televised election debates are extremely accurate:<br><br><blockquote>
<br>'I will award three points to Mr Kaine for an excellent nonspecific condemnation, plus one bonus point for blaming the previous government, and another for successfully mutating the question to promote the party line. Mr van de Poste gets a point for a firm rebuttal, but only two points for his condemnation as he tried to inject an impartial and intelligent observation.'<br>
</blockquote><br><br>I contamplated giving it a rating of 2/5, but the extremely satisfying ending tacked on an extra star. It would've been good enough to wrap-up the entire series... had <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde" title="Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">Jasper Fforde</a> decided to end the series here. Luckily for fans, that's not the case. I, however, will be taking an indefinite break from the books.<br><br><strong>3/5 stars</strong> for yet another funny and quotable book from the Thursday Next series.<br>==========================================<br>Review of the 2nd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/974447586" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost in a Good Book</a><br>Review of the 3rd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1072313241" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Lost Plots</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19175224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3166077060311455450">This took me a LONG time to get into. It has been on my "to-read" list since 2008, so for a while I wondered why I even bothered. I started enjoying it about half way through, and then I came across a passage that made the whole thing worth it:<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/>"Wait!" I cried out. <br/>"What?" <br/>"I can't concentrate with all those people!"<br/>Landen looked around the empty bedroom. "What people?"<br/>"Those people," I repeated, waving a hand in the general direction of everywhere, "the ones <i>reading</i> us."<br/>Landen sta</span></span>
  <span id="freeText3166077060311455450" style="display:none">This took me a LONG time to get into. It has been on my "to-read" list since 2008, so for a while I wondered why I even bothered. I started enjoying it about half way through, and then I came across a passage that made the whole thing worth it:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />"Wait!" I cried out. <br />"What?" <br />"I can't concentrate with all those people!"<br />Landen looked around the empty bedroom. "What people?"<br />"Those people," I repeated, waving a hand in the general direction of everywhere, "the ones <i>reading</i> us."<br />Landen stared at me and raised an eyebrow. I felt stupid, then relaxed and gave out a nervous giggle.<br />"Sorry. I've been living inside fiction for too long; sometimes I get this weird feeling that you, me and everything else are just...well, characters in a book or something."<br />"Plainly, that is ridiculous."<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />When I read it, I laughed out loud, and it made me feel like she was looking right at me! I put a marker in the page so I could read it again, which I did several times and enjoyed chuckling each time. I even had to share the passage with my husband.<br /><br />By the end of the book, I was really enjoying it. If I jump into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27002.First_Among_Sequels__Thursday_Next___5_" title="First Among Sequels (Thursday Next, #5) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">First Among Sequels</a> right away, maybe it won't take me so long to get into the story and remember the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3166077060311455450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10249432029723118866">After belong a little disappointed by the third book, this one was back in the 'real world', and just as much fun as the first two.<br/>The plot was deliberately complex, full of twists and turns. Nevertheless I found it easy to understand as events follow their own internal logic.<br/><br/>The bad people were vanquished, the good people won (but not without cost), the funny characters amused, and the dodos waddled in occasionally to do their dodo thing.<br/><br/>By the end of the book the major story lines were resolve</span>
  <span id="freeText10249432029723118866" style="display:none">After belong a little disappointed by the third book, this one was back in the 'real world', and just as much fun as the first two.<br />The plot was deliberately complex, full of twists and turns. Nevertheless I found it easy to understand as events follow their own internal logic.<br /><br />The bad people were vanquished, the good people won (but not without cost), the funny characters amused, and the dodos waddled in occasionally to do their dodo thing.<br /><br />By the end of the book the major story lines were resolved in ways that were both dramatic and humorous, while enough minor questions were left open to allow for further adventures.<br /><br />A very satisfying read. I will certainly read the next one.<br /><br />BTW, I thought the Brought-Vincent-Norton motorcycle factory was a Triumph.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText3087055905408788350" style="display:none">This might be my favorite book of the series. Time travel gives me a headache but Fforde handles it very well across this series, and the inclusion of classic characters remains a joy. (I still need a Mrs Tiggy-Winkle figurine for my bookshelf. Christmas, anyone?) The one mistake I made after Well of Lost Plots was to go reading about Thursday Next on Wikipedia -- spoilered myself for Granny Next, but that actually resolved itself in this book! Huzzah! And it was quite... I feel like I've used "unexpectedly poignant" too recently to bust it out again, but... yes. <br /><br />At any rate, I love these books and I love Jasper's imagination. Each of these books feels like a cobbled-together NaNoWriMo project, and personally it gives me much hope when NaNoWriMo rolls around each year.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11951948-paul?shelf=books-read-2014">books-read-2014</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer726186132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15060477791016644689">Two years have passed and Thursday is still working in Jurisfiction and hunting the Minotaur, but she longs to return to the real world and find Landen, previously eradicated by the Goliath Corporation. Her son Friday is now two<br/><br/>She returns to Swindon with Hamlet, who wants to see what the real world is like and stays with her mother and father. She gets her job back at SpecOps and starts to find out all she has missed. President George Formby is still in power but the Goliath Corporation has mad</span>
  <span id="freeText15060477791016644689" style="display:none">Two years have passed and Thursday is still working in Jurisfiction and hunting the Minotaur, but she longs to return to the real world and find Landen, previously eradicated by the Goliath Corporation. Her son Friday is now two<br /><br />She returns to Swindon with Hamlet, who wants to see what the real world is like and stays with her mother and father. She gets her job back at SpecOps and starts to find out all she has missed. President George Formby is still in power but the Goliath Corporation has made allegiances with Yorrick Kaine and plan to oust him. Kaine has growing power and influence and is using it to stir up hatred of Denmark, and has sought the services of 'The Windowmaker' (a spelling mistake, but it was too late to correct) an assassin who turns out to be the wife of a friends of hers.<br /><br />She meets with the CEO of the Goliath Corporation to try again to get Landen back, and they promise that they will for her forgiveness, but she is convinced that she has had some mind control applied. Landedn appears, but it takes a while for reality to get used to him being there so he keeps disappearing. Her father, now re-admitted to the time-travelling ChronoGuard, warns her of the perils that Kaine's plan pose. Along with the Goliath Corporation planning to become a religion to avoid the prophecy that they are doomed to fail, and that Thursday has to get the Swindon Mallets to win the 1988 Croquet Superhoop to avoid the end of the world, her biggest problem is getting childcare.<br /><br />Not quite as good as the previous one the the series, it didn't seem to have the focus of the last. That said, I do like the way that Fforde writes these, they are cleverly done, and full of wit and ideas and sub plots that turn and twist.</span>

  <span id="freeText17964397592070463869" style="display:none">I started this series actually with the second book, because we read it at an English course at University.           <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926197210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13988884490868494447">The fourth (4th) book in the Thursday Next series.<br/><br/>THIS WILL CONTAIN SPOILERS FOR PREVIOUS BOOKS IN THE SERIES.<br/><br/>Thursday Next is living in Bookworld. She is one of the rare, rare people with the ability to read herself into books. Now she is The Bellman - the sort of leader in charge of Bookworld. She spends her days calming fictional characters, stopping character rebellion, and keeping plotlines stable. She has a two-year-old son, the boy Friday. Her husband and one true love, Landon, is eradica</span>
  <span id="freeText13988884490868494447" style="display:none">The fourth (4th) book in the Thursday Next series.<br /><br />THIS WILL CONTAIN SPOILERS FOR PREVIOUS BOOKS IN THE SERIES.<br /><br />Thursday Next is living in Bookworld. She is one of the rare, rare people with the ability to read herself into books. Now she is The Bellman - the sort of leader in charge of Bookworld. She spends her days calming fictional characters, stopping character rebellion, and keeping plotlines stable. She has a two-year-old son, the boy Friday. Her husband and one true love, Landon, is eradicated - Chronoguard in the real world went back in time and killed him when he was just 2-years-old, winking him out of existence.<br /><br />She's been hiding out in Bookworld to save her son and so that she survived her pregnancy (a lot of people in the real world want her dead) but she knows it's time to face the music. She must go back into the real world and get her husband back. She brings Shakespeare's Hamlet back with her. So Thursday, Friday, Hamlet, and Thursday's pet dodos start on their quest to recover Landon.<br /><br />This book is very hard for me to summarize or describe. It involves the "real people" such as Thursday, her parents, her aunt and uncle, her dodos (extinct pets are all the rage!) and her son Friday. However, the book is also cast with famous fictional characters, real and imagined, such as Hamlet, the Cheshire Cat, the Minotaur, the Kraken, etc. etc. <br /><br />The book is very funny and very smart. It is truly a book for book lovers. However, a caveat - if you haven't read all the classics or are a bit lacking in your knowledge of literature a lot of the jokes will go over your head. I personally enjoy these books very much and Thursday Next is a strong female character that I admire.<br /><br />P.S. This book is illustrated. I get a kick out of adult books with illustrations in them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13988884490868494447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5210117?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780340825976" href="/book/show/1298315.Something_Rotten">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/310403-kyle?shelf=re-reading">re-reading</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5210117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3699068702212847765">Happy birthday, William Shakespeare, and as a gift for your 450th, I present to you an excellent book written for your 440th. Jasper Fforde has exactly the same love of reading and writer's inventiveness as many of the great ones who are inspired by your creativity. Not only does he give Hamlet some thoughtful reflection upon his role as a dithering protagonist, but also literally brings you back to life with all the tragic consequences of your great plays. Okay, not even <em>King Lear</em> suggests an a</span>
  <span id="freeText3699068702212847765" style="display:none">Happy birthday, William Shakespeare, and as a gift for your 450th, I present to you an excellent book written for your 440th. Jasper Fforde has exactly the same love of reading and writer's inventiveness as many of the great ones who are inspired by your creativity. Not only does he give Hamlet some thoughtful reflection upon his role as a dithering protagonist, but also literally brings you back to life with all the tragic consequences of your great plays. Okay, not even <em>King Lear</em> suggests an armageddon like <em>Something Rotten</em>'s threat of global nuclear warfare, and you certainly held back on the puns and cartoon-like violence. Beyond this surreal alternate reality surface is that mirror held up to nature for those who have "drunk ink," as it were.<br /><br />In case you "had left vnſeene a wonderfull peece of worke" known as Thursday Next, allow me to explain how much she fits in with the thousands and thousands of inspired characters derived from your plays. First of all, she has met with and worked alongside many many of literature's brightest stars, but is level-headed and pragmatic in an otherwise chaotic fictional world. Returning to her home world to find, as the title suggests, things rotten in Swindon, she takes on as many of these burdens as she can manage, never being crushed by the responsibility nor the silly wordplay. No matter how much she seems to know about the future and events in the past that went otherwise, she knows of the urgency to do the right thing when the time comes. And only at the midpoint of her highly entertaining series, each novel she is in feels like her story is just beginning to unfold. Finally, although she is based upon so many wonderful parts, Thursday has the one quality you seem to enjoy most: originality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3699068702212847765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText280198582610595920" style="display:none">This was book №4 in the Thursday next series, and although a lot of loose threads from the previous books came together, for me this book just didn't read as well as the others. There was a fair amount of repetition which went on, which seemed to interupt the flow of the storyline. Once again the multiple threads reminded me of the plate spinners from the old variety acts.<br />Time has moved on and Thursday exits the Bookworld to reappear in the real world. She is accompanied by her 2 year old son, Shakespeare's Hamlet, and two Dodos. Once again she locks horns with the Goliath Corporation, and an odious individual, Yorrick Kaine. Faced with trying to sort out her bank overdraft she tries to regain her old job in SpecOps. Time has progressed but I never feel that Thursday has continued to develop past the first couple of books.<br />There is mayhem aplenty in both worlds, and at times the plots do enter into the fantastical, so sometimes you do have to ignore certain things and just go with the flow. </span>

    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3673987-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576635887p2/3673987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/367956392?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/3673987-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3673987-mike?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer367956392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8890339664449036013">TN4: I enjoyed it less than the first three -- it was a 'helicopter', a lot of unrelated parts moving in synchrony, that yet somehow seem to get the story from point A to point B. However, we get a few answers! (Of course, it would be a spoiler to give them all away. But, gingham? Really?) It has a lot to recommend it to the literophile, especially fans of the Revernd Dodgson (I really hope I spelled his name correctly. Oh, wait -- I'm on the <i>Internet!</i></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_119460871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119460871" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119460871?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670033591" href="/book/show/107378.Something_Rotten">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy-arcanepunk">fantasy-arcanepunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119460871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7997489219288587884">Fourth in the Thursday Next arcanepunk fantasy series and revolving around a book operative and her search for her husband. Oh, and saving the world. It’s 1988 and set in Swindon, Wessex, England.<br/><br/>In 2005, <em>Something Rotten</em> was nominated for the Dilys Award.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>It’s not fair. I wanna go journeying around inside books… And I wonder if we could get some Narrative Assumption out here. Be darned handy when you don’t want to go shopping or brush your hair.<br/><br/>There are conflicts up the wazoo with a mill</span>
  <span id="freeText7997489219288587884" style="display:none">Fourth in the Thursday Next arcanepunk fantasy series and revolving around a book operative and her search for her husband. Oh, and saving the world. It’s 1988 and set in Swindon, Wessex, England.<br /><br />In 2005, <em>Something Rotten</em> was nominated for the Dilys Award.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />It’s not fair. I wanna go journeying around inside books… And I wonder if we could get some Narrative Assumption out here. Be darned handy when you don’t want to go shopping or brush your hair.<br /><br />There are conflicts up the wazoo with a million beats. Well, there must be a million, there’s so much action goin' on! You won’t be bored, that’s for sure. The amazing thing is that while most of the assorted conflicts are heading off in a variety of directions, they actually come back together at the end. Including a few I had never expected!<br /><br />I do adore Fforde’s Thursday Next. It’s a whole ‘nother look at books…and the “truth” of what goes on in the book world. And you thought you knew… I’ll confess that I had no idea how wild and woolly those characters can be. But I can understand getting bored doing the same thing day after day.<br /><br />Then there’s Fforde’s explanations...er, I mean, Fforde's use of first person protagonist point-of-view to explain how much work the reader does, as “they clothe the author’s description with the memory of their own experiences”. It does make sense that this would make every book unique for each reader. And unique each time the reader reads the book! On the other end of it, Hamlet makes a good point about what a lousy book the real world would make, lol. And then Thursday freaks out about all the people reading her and Land…until she realizes she’s not in BookWorld anymore. <em>Uh-huh</em>…<br /><br />We do get an up-close-and-personal with what makes Hamlet tick. Teachers should check this out to see how they could incorporate this into studying <em>Hamlet</em>. It would certainly make the kids think. Unfortunately, there’s been a hostile takeover in <em>Hamlet</em>, so...the story may not be there anymore.<br /><br />Friday is a crack-up with his Lorem Ipsum chatter. So is the new face of Goliath. Oh, brother. Goliath is consistent in their hypocrisy. I gotta give 'em that. As for those character names, omigod, way too funny. <em>When you get down to the characters, sound some of them out. You will C-R-A-C-K up.</em> There's something to be said for using names to describe a character *more laughter*<br /><br />Oh lord, the politics in this are even crazier than the storyline. What’s worse? They sound like our own politicians!! The politicians, okay, <em>Kaine</em>, is shoving the Danes under the bus and no one knows why…until the end, anyway.<br /><br />It was coming. Yep, performance-enhancing drugs for novelists. And Melanie gives us the backstory on how she met Trafford.<br /><br />Theme-wise...oh, lordy. We're talkin' "wazoo" again. What with Thursday's will to survive and her intention to knock back the greedy Goliath, the role religion plays in this — lolololol, the wacky technology, and the blessings of family and friends, there is plenty to go around.<br /><br />The culture that Fforde created for those neanderthals. Too funny. Actually the whole concept of Thursday Next, SpecOps, and Jurisfiction is an amazing set of cultures. I sure wouldn’t have thought books could be so busy outside their own stories.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Thursday Next is about to be arrested for her part in that international cheese-smuggling scandal AND for being absent without leave! Luckily, her stickler of a boss has finally had it.<br /><br />That's the easy part of Thursday's life. With Hamlet in Outland, the lesser characters in <em>Hamlet</em> have staged a takeover, and the play is becoming <em>The Merry Wives of Elsinore</em>. Thursday badly needs a Shakespeare! On another front, Yorrick Kaine is trying to take over the government...the country...the world! And if Thursday wants Landen back, she'll have to confront the newly religious Goliath.<br /><br />Then there's that unlikely Seventh Revealment. If the Mallets don't win...it'll be Armageddon. And who will babysit her son while Thursday saves the world?<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Thursday “Doofus” Next</strong> is the Bellman of Jurisfiction, but will end up as the SO-14 Danish Book Seizure Liaison Officer. <strong>Friday</strong> is her two-year-old son whose father is the eradicated <strong>Landen Parke-Laine</strong> (<em>his</em> mother is <strong>Houson</strong>). <strong>Poley</strong> is Friday’s stuffed polar bear. <strong>Pickwick “Pickers”</strong> is her cloned dodo; the naughty <strong>Alan</strong> is Pickwick's son.<br /><br /><strong>Lady Emma Hamilton</strong> is in the spare room; <strong>Mum</strong> — <em>she does a very nice Battenberg cake</em> — thinks her husband is having it off with Emma! <strong>Otto Bismarck</strong>, the Prussian Chancellor, is in the attic, and Mum seems to be considering an affair. <strong>Dad</strong> is a time-traveler, but no longer with ChronoGuard. <strong>Mrs. Beatty</strong> is the next-door neighbor.<br /><br />The <strong>Very Irreverent Joffy Next</strong> is Thursday’s brother and a minister in the <strong>Global Standard Deity</strong> religion. He’s also the head of the Idolatry Friends of St. Zvlkx. <b>Miles</b> is his life partner. <strong>Uncle Mycroft and Aunt Polly Next</strong> are brilliant inventors currently at the Fourteenth Annual Mad Scientists’ Conference. Their sons, <strong>Wilbur</strong> and <strong>Orville</strong>, are not living up to their parents’ intelligence.<br /><br /><em>Goliath Twilight Homes is…</em><br />…an old folks’ home where <strong>Granny Next</strong> is living. <em>She has a preference for blue gingham and insists she can’t die until she’s read the ten most boring books.</em><br /><br /><em>Jurisfiction is…</em><br />…a policing agency <em>inside</em> BookWorld with Prose Resource Operatives working to maintain the continuity of the narrative in every book ever written. Its head is the <strong>Bellman</strong>. <em>
  <strong>The Sword of the Zenobians</strong>
</em> is an unpublished work used as a prison.<br /><br /><strong>Commander Trafford Bradshaw</strong> is retired as the lead character of the Commander Bradshaw novels — no one’s read them since 1963. Now he’s a most welcome Jurisfiction agent. <strong>Melanie Bradshaw</strong>, a mountain gorilla, is his wife; she gets along very well with Friday. <strong>Emperor Zhark</strong> is from his own series (written by <strong>Handley Paige</strong>) and is a Jurisfiction agent as well. He tends to go over the top. Part of it, Thursday thinks, is due to his mother, <strong>Empress Zharkeena</strong>.<strong> Mrs. Tiggy-winkle</strong> is a hedgehog who is one of three people in charge. The <strong>Red Queen</strong> will only police anything before 1867. <strong>Vernham Deane</strong> is a busy cad. The <strong>Cat Formerly Known as Cheshire</strong>, an überlibrarian, is in charge of the Great Library (only his mother can call him <em>Archibald</em>). The <strong>Gryphon</strong> is an excellent lawyer and working on Thursday’s appeal. <strong>Mock Turtle</strong> is his number two.<br /><br /><em> BookWorld is...</em><br />...the world within books and is ruled by the <strong>Council of Genres</strong>, which is made up of a representative from every genre, and they decide the conventions of storytelling. The <strong>Well</strong>, located beneath the <strong>Great Library</strong> where all published fiction is stored, is where books are constructed. <strong>Daphne Farquitt</strong> has written over 500 really awful romances, including <em>At Long Last Lust</em>.<br /> Swindon, Wessex, England, is… <br />…Thursday’s home town. <strong>Prince Hamlet of Denmark</strong> is visiting the Outland as part of an appeasement process, as Jurisfiction is hoping he’ll sign on to police Elizabethan drama. While visiting Thursday, he’ll be known as <strong>Cousin Eddie</strong>. <strong>Ophelia</strong> is his girlfriend. <strong>St. Zvlkx</strong> is Swindon’s very own saint from the thirteenth century and his <strong>Revealments</strong> are quite popular. <strong>Lady Volescamper</strong> is the mayor’s wife. <strong>Mrs. Barnet</strong> is the chief hairstylist (and gossip) at Mum’s hairdresser's.<br /><br /><em>SpecOps (Special Operations Network) in…</em><br />…Swindon was where Thursday’s old job was. They police areas too specialized for the regular police. The golf-mad <strong>Commander Braxton Hicks</strong> was her unhappy, by-the-books boss over at <strong>SO-27, the Literary Detectives</strong>. <strong>Victor Analogy</strong> is another old boss. <strong>Bowden Cable</strong> is Thursday’s old partner. <strong>Joe Martlet</strong> was killed by the Cheese Mafia.<br /><br /><strong>Bartholomew "Stiggs" Stiggins</strong>, a neanderthal, is head of <b>SO-13, the cloning police</b>. <strong>Felicity</strong> is his life partner. All the neanderthals in Swindon live in a village known as the <strong>Nation</strong>. Since <strong>neanderthals</strong> were legally reengineered by Goliath, that corporation technically owns him and his fellows. <em>Whew, wait’ll you read the explanation about the </em>why<em> of the neanderthal experiment.</em> <strong>Mr. Richard Dixon</strong>, a first year student at Chipping Sodbury College for Politicians, appreciates the training the ‘thals can give him.<br /><br /><strong>Major Dragg</strong> is with <strong>SO-14 (Danish Book Seizure)</strong> and assigned to help Thursday track down that pernicious Danish literature. <strong>Spike Stoker</strong> is an operative at <strong>SO-17, the Vampire and Werewolf Disposal Operations</strong>, and a friend of Thursday’s. <strong>Colonel Flanker</strong> is with <strong>SO-1, Internal Affairs</strong>. <strong>Officer Jodrell</strong> is one of his agents. <strong>SO-12 is ChronoGuard</strong>, charged with maintaining the integrity of the Standard History Eventline. <strong>Malcolm</strong> is one of its agents. <strong>Mr. Rumplunkett</strong> is the head pathologist. <strong>SO-6 is national security</strong>, and they protect the president and other high-falutin’ politicians. <strong>Colonel Parks</strong> is head of Presidential Security with <strong>Dowding</strong> as second-in-command.<br /><br /><strong>Millon de Floss</strong> is Thursday’s authorized stalker, and he is a conspiracy theorist. <strong>Adam Gnusense</strong>, a Grade-3, is Millon’s stalker.<br /><br /><em>The Swindon Mallets are…</em><br />…the town’s croquet team with <strong>Roger Kapok</strong> as captain. <strong>Aubrey Jambe</strong> is hoop defense, <strong>Alan “Biffo” Mandible</strong> plays midfield, <strong>“Smudger” Blarney</strong> is a forward hoop, <strong>Laura de Rematte</strong> was their top defender, <strong>"Snake" Spillikin</strong> is a forward striker, <strong>George</strong>, and <strong>Johnno Swift</strong>. <strong>Penelope Hrah</strong> joins the team as the midhoop wingman. The neanderthals who agree to play include <strong>Stiggs</strong> as a racquet taker, <strong>Grunk</strong> is on defense, <strong>Dorf</strong> is peg defense, and <strong>Zim</strong> is a striker. <strong>Gray Ferguson</strong> had been their manager. <strong>Runcorn &amp; Twizitt</strong> is their legal team. <strong>Alf Widdershaine</strong> is Thursday’s record-holding old croquet coach.<br /><br />They’ll be up against the <strong>Reading Whackers</strong> (they’ve signed ace player <strong>Bonecrusher McSneed</strong> to play forward hoop) in the <strong>SuperHoop 88</strong>. <strong>George “Rhino” McNasty</strong> ends up doing community service. T<strong>im O’Fathens</strong> is the Whackers captain; the <strong>Duchess of Sheffield</strong> is a wingman. Their legal team is <strong>Wapcaplitt &amp; Sfortz</strong>.<br /><br /><strong>Wilson Lonsdale &amp; Partners</strong> are England's top sports agents.<br /><br /><em>Eradications Anonymous is…</em><br />…a self-help group for people with severe memory aberrations to which Mum belongs. <strong>Julie Aseizer</strong> had been a member but then her <strong>Ralph</strong> showed up.<br /><br /><em>The British government</em><br /><strong>President George Formby</strong> does not like <strong>Yorrick Kaine</strong> (<em>he's an escaped fictionaut hiding in the Outland and in league with the Goliath Corporation, shhh</em>). And Kaine is currently the English Chancellor with a yen to be dictator. <strong>Colonel Fawsten Gayle</strong> is head of Kaine’s security. <strong>Ernst Stricknene</strong> is Kaine’s personal advisor. <strong>Robert Edsel</strong> is the Kainian minister of road safety *eye roll*. <strong>Redmond van de Poste</strong>, the Opposition leader, is the leader of the Commonsense Party and sponsored by the Toast Marketing Board; he’s taking over from the deceased <strong>Mrs. Fay Bentoss</strong>.<br /><br /><em>Evade the Question Time is…</em><br />…a topical talk show on <strong>ToadNews-Network</strong> hosted by <strong>Tudor Webastow</strong> of <em>The Owl</em>. Audience members include <strong>Miss Pupkin</strong>, <strong>Miss Ives</strong>, and <strong>Mr. Wedgwood</strong>. Another talk show is <em>
  <strong>Swindon Breakfast with Toad</strong>
</em> with <strong>Warwick Fridge</strong> and <strong>Leigh Onzolent</strong>. <strong>Lydia Startright</strong> is an on-air reporter.<br /><br /><em>Goliath Corporation is…</em><br />…truly evil, even more evil than the usual multinational corporation and based on the Isle of Man. The town of Laxey has been renamed <strong>Goliathopolis</strong>. And now they’re switching to a faith-based corporate management system. <strong>Sister Bettina of Stroud</strong> is their corporate precog. <strong>Mr. Cheese</strong> and <strong>Mr. Chalk</strong> are corporate bullies. <strong>Brik Schitt-Hawse</strong> heads up the tech division and does something with Uncle Mycroft’s Ovinator! <strong>Mr. Toedee</strong> is the head of PR. <strong>Jack Schitt</strong> has been demoted far, far down the ladder from his former position as head of Goliath’s Advanced Weapons Division. <strong>Mr. Higgs</strong> is his assistant. <strong>Mr. Godfrey</strong> is the CEO’s personal assistant’s assistant. <strong>John Henry Goliath V</strong> is the CEO and great-great-grandson of Goliath’s founder. <strong>Mr. Jarvis</strong> is on the board and coming up with all sorts of reasons why buying Antarctica was a good deal.<br /><br /><em>Death at Double-X Ranch…</em><br />…is a pulp western that is set in 1878 and written in 1908. <strong>Howell</strong> is a drunk. <strong>Abel Baxter</strong> wants a gunfight with the sheriff. <strong>McNeil</strong> rode into town at the wrong time.<br /><br />The <strong>Minotaur</strong>, a half-man, half-bull, escaped two years ago in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27001.The_Well_of_Lost_Plots" target="_blank" title="Opens Jasper Fforde's The Well of Lost Plots in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Well of Lost Plots</em>
</a>, 3; he may be traveling under the alias, <strong>Norman Johnson</strong>.<br /><br />The <strong>Outland</strong> is our world. <strong>Horatio Nelson</strong> seems to want to die. <strong>Samuel Pring</strong> had been a politician. A <strong>Glatisant</strong> is a fictional hell beast. The <strong>Windowmaker</strong> is an assassin. She’s also <strong>Cindy</strong>, a Sicilian librarian, who is married to Spike, and they have a year-old daughter, <strong>Betty</strong>. Her brother is a librarian for the CIA. <strong>Mr. Wentworth</strong> is a fan of Thursday's. Other Hamlets include <strong>Piarno Keyes</strong> playing the character. <strong>Pete &amp; Dave’s</strong> is a local reengineered-pet store. <strong>Dennis</strong> was the chimera at the mall. <strong>Mr. Tork Armada</strong> is the spokesman for OFGOD, the religious-institution-licensing authority, and he is <em>not</em> impressed with Goliath’s ratings. <strong>Daisy Mutlar</strong> was the woman Landen nearly married. A <strong>grammasite</strong> is a parasitic life-form that lives inside books. <strong>Dave Chesney</strong> is Spike’s old partner from SO-17. <strong>Mr. Martin Piffco</strong> tells the truth and is committed for it. <em>I wonder how long we have before we’re committed for speaking against the government…or a politician…</em> <strong>Rupert Smercc</strong> of Ipswich isn’t too pleased, either. <strong>Mr. Pascoe</strong> is the official spokesman for the Federated Agnostics.<strong> St. Septyk’s Hospital</strong>.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The background of the cover has a close-up swirl of cloud with watercolor shadows of deep blue fading into the white of the paper. In the bottom half is a hardcover book open to reveal a cut-out in which resides a piece of toast with too, too-clever holes that remind me of a skull. It is a cute way to announce the series information. Text-wise, there’s an info blurb at the very top using the same red as the book. Below that is the author’s name in a royal blue sans-serif font. The title, in a teal green script font, is between the author and the book.<br /><br />The title refers to the political situation, where there is <em>Something Rotten</em>, but it is not in the state of Denmark.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7997489219288587884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_235029174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235029174" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6946107-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483280158p2/6946107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235029174?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/6946107-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer235029174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11213380035315852119">It's two years after the events of the previous book, and Thursday is back in the real world, with her son, Friday, and the two dodos, Pickwick and Alan, in tow. Oh, and Hamlet, who's been given a chance to visit the Outland to try and stop him dithering so much. Thursday discovers that Chancellor Yorrick Kane is trying to start a war with Denmark, that St Zvlkx, thirteenth century prophet, is due to arrive at his Second Coming in Swindon, and that Landon is still eradicated. Caught up in politi</span>
  <span id="freeText11213380035315852119" style="display:none">It's two years after the events of the previous book, and Thursday is back in the real world, with her son, Friday, and the two dodos, Pickwick and Alan, in tow. Oh, and Hamlet, who's been given a chance to visit the Outland to try and stop him dithering so much. Thursday discovers that Chancellor Yorrick Kane is trying to start a war with Denmark, that St Zvlkx, thirteenth century prophet, is due to arrive at his Second Coming in Swindon, and that Landon is still eradicated. Caught up in political machinations, gaining a stalker and a would-be assassin, and trying to find a babysitter while ensuring a prophecy is fulfilled, handling occasional Bookworld problems, and dealing with her job back at SpecOps, Thursday is beset from all sides.<br /><br />I don't usually include quotations in my reviews, but this just made me laugh so hard, I couldn't resist:<br /><br /><cite>I was woken by Pickwick wanting to be let out, and Alan wanting to be let in. The smaller dodo had some paint spilled on him, smelt of perfume, had a blue ribbon tied around his left foot and was holding a mackerel in his beak. I have no idea to this day what he's been getting up to.</cite><br /><br />I don't know why, but I find the dodos so funny. They're brilliant. The combination of bewildered Pickwick and reprobate Alan is just superb. St Zvlkx is amusing too, with all his speech (mainly swearing) typeset in a gothic font. There's a whole heap of other humour too, much more on the political satire side this time, and the main plot threads are all tied off neatly by the end. Much fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11213380035315852119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('crsC82jfEBVSpZa1uYxurzFhE9zaBo1Y1RTCUAnd49l5o5fe/rPumMc3ex8uMvpG/iRdpdpzqjjilpYrjtL5lA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

Dès 2 ans, les enfants des pays occidentaux cumulent chaque jour presque 3 heures d\'écran. Entre 8 et 12 ans, ils passent à près de 4 h 45. Entre 13 et 18 ans, ils frôlent les 6 h 45. En cumuls annuels, ces usages représentent autour de 1 000 heures pour un élève de maternelle (soit davantage que le volume horaire d\'une année scolaire), 1 700 heures pour un écolier de cours moyen (2 années scolaires) et 2 400 heures pour un lycéen du secondaire (2,5 années scolaires). Contrairement à certaines idées reçues, cette profusion d\'écrans est loin d\'améliorer les aptitudes de nos enfants. Bien au contraire, elle a de lourdes conséquences : sur la santé (obésité, développement cardio-vasculaire, espérance de vie réduite...), sur le comportement (agressivité, dépression, conduites à risques...) et sur les capacités intellectuelles (langage, concentration, mémorisation...). Autant d\'atteintes qui affectent fortement la réussite scolaire des jeunes. &quot; Ce que nous faisons subir à nos enfants est inexcusable. Jamais sans doute, dans l\'histoire de l\'humanité, une telle expérience de décérébration n\'avait été conduite à aussi grande échelle &quot;, estime Michel Desmurget. Ce livre, première synthèse des études scientifiques internationales sur les effets réels des écrans, est celui d\'un homme en colère. La conclusion est sans appel : attention écrans, poisons lents ! Michel Desmurget est docteur en neurosciences et directeur de recherche à l\'Inserm.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde">About Jasper Fforde</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1528718375p3/4432.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde">Jasper Fforde
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
10,442
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13599291387309448431">Fforde began his career in the film industry, and for nineteen years held a variety of posts on such movies as Goldeneye, The Mask of Zorro and Entrapment. Secretly harbouring a desire to tell his own stories rather than help other people tell their's, Jasper started writing in 1988, and spent eleven years secretly writing novel after novel as he strove to find a style of his own that was a no-man</span>
  <span id="freeText13599291387309448431" style="display:none">Fforde began his career in the film industry, and for nineteen years held a variety of posts on such movies as Goldeneye, The Mask of Zorro and Entrapment. Secretly harbouring a desire to tell his own stories rather than help other people tell their's, Jasper started writing in 1988, and spent eleven years secretly writing novel after novel as he strove to find a style of his own that was a no-mans-land somewhere between the warring factions of Literary and Absurd.<br /><br />After receiving 76 rejection letters from publishers, Jasper's first novel The Eyre Affair was taken on by Hodder &amp; Stoughton and published in July 2001. Set in 1985 in a world that is similar to our own, but with a few crucial - and bizarre - differences (Wales is a socialist republic, the Crimean War is still ongoing and the most popular pets are home-cloned dodos), The Eyre Affair introduces literary detective named 'Thursday Next'. Thursday's job includes spotting forgeries of Shakespeare's lost plays, mending holes in narrative plot lines, and rescuing characters who have been kidnapped from literary masterpieces.<br /><br />Luckily for Jasper, the novel garnered dozens of effusive reviews, and received high praise from the press, from booksellers and readers throughout the UK. In the US The Eyre Affair was also an instant hit, entering the New York Times Bestseller List in its first week of publication. <br /><br />Since then, Jasper has added another six to the Thursday Next series and has also begun a second series that he calls 'Nursery Crime', featuring Jack Spratt of The Nursery Crime Division. In the first book, 'The Big Over Easy', Humpty Dumpty is the victim in a whodunnit, and in the second, 'The Fourth Bear', the Three Bear's connection to Goldilocks disappearance can finally be revealed. <br /><br />In January 2010 Fforde published 'Shades of Grey', in which a fragmented society struggle to survive in a colour-obsessed post-apocalyptic landscape. <br /><br />His latest series is for Young Adults and include 'The Last Dragonslayer' (2010), 'Song of the Quarkbeast' (2011) and 'The Eye of Zoltar' (2013). All the books centre around Jennifer Strange, who manages a company of magicians named 'Kazam', and her attempts to keep the noble arts from the clutches of big business and property tycoons.<br /><br />Jasper's 14th Book, 'Early Riser', a thriller set in a world in which humans have always hibernated, is due out in the UK in August 2018, and in the US in 2019.<br /><br />Fforde failed his Welsh Nationality Test by erroneously identifying Gavin Henson as a TV chef, but continues to live and work in his adopted nation despite this setback. He has a Welsh wife, two welsh daughters and a welsh dog, who is mad but not because he's Welsh. He has a passion for movies, photographs, and aviation. (Jasper, not the dog)<br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43680-thursday-next" rel="nofollow noopener">Thursday Next</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43679-nursery-crime" rel="nofollow noopener">Nursery Crime</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51553-shades-of-grey" rel="nofollow noopener">Shades of Grey</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13599291387309448431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
